###begin article-title 0
Investigation of catalysis by bacterial RNase P via LNA and other modifications at the scissile phosphodiester
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Present address: Dr Simona Cuzic-Feltens, Martin-Luther Universitat Halle, Institut fur Biochemie und Biotechnologie, Kurt-Mothes Strasse, 306120 Halle (Saale), Germany.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 59 60 59 60 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 301 302 301 302 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 311 327 311 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 440 444 440 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">endo</italic>
###xml 527 528 527 528 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 574 575 574 575 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 575 576 575 576 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 597 599 597 599 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 697 698 697 698 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 704 706 704 706 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 756 758 756 758 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 776 777 776 777 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 786 788 786 788 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 845 846 845 846 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 919 920 919 920 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 983 985 983 985 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 311 327 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
We analyzed cleavage of precursor tRNAs with an LNA, 2'-OCH3, 2'-H or 2'-F modification at the canonical (c0) site by bacterial RNase P. We infer that the major function of the 2'-substituent at nt -1 during substrate ground state binding is to accept an H-bond. Cleavage of the LNA substrate at the c0 site by Escherichia coli RNase P RNA demonstrated that the transition state for cleavage can in principle be achieved with a locked C3' -endo ribose and without the H-bond donor function of the 2'-substituent. LNA and 2'-OCH3 suppressed processing at the major aberrant m-1 site; instead, the m+1 (nt +1/+2) site was utilized. For the LNA variant, parallel pathways leading to cleavage at the c0 and m+1 sites had different pH profiles, with a higher Mg2+ requirement for c0 versus m+1 cleavage. The strong catalytic defect for LNA and 2'-OCH3 supports a model where the extra methylene (LNA) or methyl group (2'-OCH3) causes a steric interference with a nearby bound catalytic Mg2+ during its recoordination on the way to the transition state for cleavage. The presence of the protein cofactor suppressed the ground state binding defects, but not the catalytic defects.
###end p 2

###xml 264 269 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 799 815 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 820 837 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">Bacillus subtilis</span>
###xml 1682 1689 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1693 1704 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 2867 2878 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Endonucleolytic 5'-end maturation of tRNA primary transcripts is catalyzed by the ribonucleoprotein enzyme Ribonuclease P (RNase P) in all three domains of life (Archaea, Bacteria and Eukarya) as well as in mitochondria and chloroplasts (1-4). An exception is the human mitochondrial tRNA 5'-end maturation enzyme that lacks an RNA subunit, with its three protein subunits recruited from related and unrelated biochemical pathways (5). Bacterial RNase P enzymes are composed of a catalytic RNA subunit (6), approximately400 nucleotides (nt) in length, and a single small protein of typically 120 amino acids (7). The protein is essential in vivo, but in vitro its absence can be compensated by increased mono- and particularly di-valent cations (6). Studies with RNase P RNA ribozymes (P RNAs) from Escherichia coli and Bacillus subtilis have indicated a specific role for at least two metal ions in productive enzyme-substrate complex formation and cleavage chemistry (8-15). Since processing of precursor tRNAs (ptRNAs) by RNase P results in cleavage products with 3'-OH and 5'-phosphate termini, an inherent feature of RNase P catalysis must be to prevent the 2'-hydroxyl group at the cleavage site from attacking the scissile phosphodiester, which would otherwise result in 5'-OH and 2',3'-cyclic phosphate ends. The 2'-hydroxyl group of the ribose at the cleavage site has indeed been identified as being crucial in the catalytic process. A 2'-deoxy or 2'-amino substitution at the canonical RNase P cleavage site (nt -1) affected substrate ground state binding, cleavage site recognition, binding of catalytically important Mg2+ and substantially reduced the cleavage rate by E. coli or B. subtilis P RNA (8,16-23). Initial evidence for the 2'-hydroxyl group at nt -1 acting as a ligand for a catalytic Mg2+ ion came from the observation that a 2'-deoxy modification at this location reduced the Hill coefficient for the Mg2+ dependence of substrate cleavage from 3 to 2 and increased the apparent Kd for Mg2+ binding 103-fold (8). A 2'-amino modification at this position resulted in miscleavage at lower pH, consistent with the idea that protonation of the 2'-amino group at lower pH causes electrostatic repulsion of a metal at this location (20,21). Mn2+ rescued cleavage at the canonical c0 site for ptRNA with a 2'-amino substitution at nt -1, which would be consistent with a direct metal ion coordination to the 2'-substituent at this location; however, a 2'-deoxy modification at the same site was rescued to a similar extent by Mn2+, thus questioning the possibility of a direct metal contact (20). We rather favor the concept of the 2'-OH at nt -1 interacting with a water molecule from the hydration shell of this metal ion (8,20). Pan and coworkers found that a 2'-deoxy substitution at the c0 cleavage site had a large effect on ptRNA cleavage by B. subtilis P RNA, whereas two in vitro selected non-tRNA substrates were little affected by such a substitution at the cleavage site; rather, the 2'-OH one nucleotide upstream was identified to be critical for cleavage of these non-tRNA substrates which lack a T stem-loop module (24). They inferred a model according to which a unique 2'-OH near the cleavage site favors a concentration-independent conformational rearrangement or docking step of initial E*S complexes [(E*S) --> (E*S)*;Scheme 1] that precedes the catalytic step. This unique 2'-OH is usually the one at the c0 site in the case of ptRNAs that are able to form the T stem-loop interaction with the P RNA S domain, but another 2'-OH in the vicinity may be utilized to fulfill this role in the absence of the T stem-loop interaction. In addition, the P protein shifts the equilibrium towards (E*S)*, thus often mitigating defects of the P RNA-alone reaction which are due to impaired (E*S)* formation. Based on this model, the 2'-OH at the c0 site in ptRNA substrates likely affects Kconf of the docking step as well as catalysis (kc0; Scheme 1). Scheme 1.Model for parallel cleavage pathways under single turnover conditions, modified based on previous models (24,51). In this example, aberrant cleavage occurs at the m+1 site. Rapid equilibria of (E*S)c0 and (E*S)m+1 commit the complexes to reaction along the different pathways. Before the bond breakage (kc0 and km+1), (E*S)c0 and (E*S)m+1 complexes are assumed to undergo a conformational rearrangement (E*S -> E*S*).
###end p 4

###xml 109 111 109 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>

###xml 312 315 312 315 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m<sub>+1</sub></sub>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 336 338 336 338 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
Model for parallel cleavage pathways under single turnover conditions, modified based on previous models (24,51). In this example, aberrant cleavage occurs at the m+1 site. Rapid equilibria of (E*S)c0 and (E*S)m+1 commit the complexes to reaction along the different pathways. Before the bond breakage (kc0 and km+1), (E*S)c0 and (E*S)m+1 complexes are assumed to undergo a conformational rearrangement (E*S -> E*S*).
###end p 5

###xml 1631 1638 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1652 1663 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 1970 1977 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2749 2756 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2761 2772 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 2839 2850 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 2858 2865 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
NMR experiments have indicated that the metal ion coordinated with the help of the 2'-OH group at nt -1 is actually 'prebound' to ptRNA before complexation with P RNA (25). In a related study, the ribose at nt -1, if not involved in base pairing, was found to be predominantly 2'-endo puckered (26), raising the possibility that a C2'-endo sugar pucker may be the favored conformation in the transition state after potential -1/73 base pairs have been disrupted through formation of the +73/294 interaction with P RNA (27). To address the role of sugar conformation at the cleavage site for the catalytic process, we analyzed a ptRNA with a locked nucleic acid (LNA) substitution at nt -1, which arrests the ribose in a C3'-endo pucker (28,29) (Figure 1). For better evaluation of effects caused by the locked ribose conformation, the loss of the H-bond donor function at the 2'-oxygen and sterical impediments due to the presence of an additional methylene group, the ptRNA variant with a 2'-OCH3 modification at this position was included in our analysis. As LNA, the 2'-OCH3 group can accept but not donate H-bonds. Unlike LNA, the 2'-OCH3 modified ribose has a flexible conformation (Table 1) and the 2'-OCH3 group can freely rotate around the C2'-O2' bond, whereas the position of the corresponding methylene is fixed in LNA. Other variants with 2'-fluoro (2'-F) or 2'-deoxy (2'-H) substitutions at nt -1 that affect the H-bonding pattern, the free energy of solvation and the electronegativity of the 2'-substituent were included as well. We then characterized the modified ptRNA substrates in reactions catalyzed by type A (E. coli) and type B (B. subtilis) RNase P (RNA) for (i) substrate ground state binding, (ii) cleavage site selection and (iii) cleavage kinetics. Our results indicate that the major function of the 2'-substitutent at nt -1 during substrate ground state binding is to accept an H-bond. We demonstrate that cleavage at the canonical site by E. coli P RNA can occur in the presence of a locked C3'-endo ribose and without the H-bond donor function of the 2'-substituent, however, with very low efficiency. The strong catalytic defect in the presence of LNA and 2'-OCH3 modifications at the c0 site supports a model where the extra methylene (LNA) or methyl group (2'-OCH3) causes a steric interference with a nearby bound catalytic Mg2+ during its recoordination on the way to the transition state for cleavage. LNA and 2'-OCH3 at the c0 site also suppressed processing at the major aberrant m-1 site, directing cleavage to the aberrant m+1 site (nt +1/+2). The protein cofactor, although suppressing the ground state binding defects, was unable to substantially relieve the severe catalytic defects. Differences between E. coli and B. subtilis enzymes included a stronger defect caused by 2'-H at nt -1 on the B. subtilis versus E. coli holoenzyme, and different cleavage site selection on the 2'-OCH3 substrate. Figure 1.(A) Secondary structure of the ptRNAGly substrate. The modified position (Y, nt -1) at the canonical (c0) RNase P cleavage site (between nt -1 and +1, marked by the arrow) is boxed. Ribose modifications are illustrated in the grey-shaded boxes on the left. Y at nt -1 represents a C or a ribo T; N at nt -2 stands for U or ribo T. The ligation site in the D-loop used for construction of different ptRNA variants is indicated by the circle. (B) Ribose sugar puckers prevailing in natural nucleic acids, from left to right: C2'-endo (type S) conformation typical of DNA in B-type helices, C3'-endo (type N) conformation typical of A-helical RNA, and the locked C3'-endo conformation in LNA; the C2'-endo and C3'-endo conformers (left and center) are shown with 2'-deoxyribose for clarity reasons.Table 1.Some physico-chemical properties of ribose moieties with different 2'-substituents2'-substituentH-bond donorH-bond acceptorFlexible ribose conformationPreferentially adopted sugar puckeraRelative solubilitybElectronegativity of 2'-substituentSterical impediments2'-OHYesYesYesC3'-endoHighestHighNoLNANoYesNoLocked C3'-endoIntermediateHighYes2'-OCH3NoYesYesC3'-endoIntermediateHighYes2'-HNoNoYesC2'-endoLowestLowNo2'-FNoYesYesC3'-endoLowHighestNoaInformation for LNA taken from Petersen et al. (52) for conformational equilibria of ribose and 2'-substituted riboses (2'-OH, 2'-H and 2'-OCH3), see Guschlbauer and Jankowski (53).bAccording to Cramer and Truhlar (54).

###xml 527 531 527 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">endo</italic>

Ribose modifications are illustrated in the grey-shaded boxes on the left. Y at nt -1 represents a C or a ribo T; N at nt -2 stands for U or ribo T. The ligation site in the D-loop used for construction of different ptRNA variants is indicated by the circle. (B) Ribose sugar puckers prevailing in natural nucleic acids, from left to right: C2'-endo (type S) conformation typical of DNA in B-type helices, C3'-endo (type N) conformation typical of A-helical RNA, and the locked C3'-endo conformation in LNA; the C2'-endo and C3'-endo conformers (left and center) are shown with 2'-deoxyribose for clarity reasons.
###end p 7

MATERIALS AND METHODS

###begin title 12
RNA synthesis, 5'-phosphorylation of RNA, 5'-end-labeling of RNA and assembly of ptRNA variants
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 78 80 78 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 213 215 213 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 216 218 216 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
Chemical and enzymatic RNA synthesis, purification, 5'-phosphorylation and 5'-32P-end-labeling of RNA, as well as the assembly of ptRNA variants with single-site modifications were performed exactly as described (20,30).

To 15 &#181;l of this solution, 1 &#181;l of P protein solution (freshly thawed and diluted) was added to adjust the solution to 0.5 &#181;M <italic>B. subtilis</italic> or 1.2 &#181;M <italic>E. coli</italic> P protein and to 125 nM P RNA, 100 mM KCl, 50 mM MES and 10 mM MgCl<sub>2</sub>, pH 6.0. ###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 17 19 17 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 47 48 47 48 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sup>

###xml 127 128 115 116 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
A solution of 5'-32P-end-labeled 24-mer RNA (104 Cerenkov cpm/microl), 0.1 microg/microl carrier RNA, 40 mM NH4OAc, 0.4 mM ZnSO4, pH 5.3 and 0.01 ng/microl nuclease P1 was incubated for 20 s at 70degreesC in a heating block. After incubation the reaction tube was placed on ice, the RNA was concentrated and desalted by ethanol precipitation and analyzed by denaturing PAGE.

###xml 1160 1161 1128 1129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 1161 1164 1129 1132 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">obs</sub>

###xml 1377 3233 1345 3189 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="24">Analysis of RNase P cleavage site selection; (<bold>A</bold>) Secondary structure of ptRNA acceptor stem ends; arrows assign the different RNase P (RNA) cleavage sites: c<sub>0</sub>, canonical site; m<sub>&#8722;</sub><sub>1</sub>, m<sub>+1</sub>, aberrant sites. (<bold>B</bold>) Cleavage of ptRNA variants LNA (T-1), 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> (T-1) and 2&#8242;-OH (T-1) by <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA (lanes 2, 4 and 6) and cleavage of the corresponding 24-mers (<xref ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>A) used to construct the ptRNA variants by nuclease P1 (lanes 1, 3 and 5). Numbers on the left side indicate the length (nt) of fragments generated by nuclease P1; the corresponding P RNA cleavage sites are indicated in parentheses. The rectangles mark the missing or reduced P1 fragments due to the absence of a 2&#8242;-OH at the corresponding position. Hydrolysis by nuclease P1 was performed as described in the &#8216;Materials and Methods&#8217; section. <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA cleavage was performed in buffer A (1 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc, 50 mM PIPES, pH 7 and 20 mM Mg<sup>2+</sup>) for 8 h (lane 2), 22 h (lane 4) and 10 min (lane 6) at 37&#176;C. (<bold>C</bold>) Analysis of cleavage site selection by <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA and holoenzyme. In lanes 1, 2, 8 and 9, processing by <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA was performed in buffer A as in panel B; cleavage by the <italic>E. coli</italic> holoenzyme (lanes 4, 5, 11 and 12) was conducted in buffer B (50 mM MES, pH 6, 0.1 M KCl and 10 mM MgCl<sub>2</sub>); we also included control reactions in buffer B in the absence of the <italic>E. coli</italic> protein subunit (lanes 6, 7, 13 and 14), which illustrate the requirement for the protein cofactor under low salt conditions: the LNA and 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> substrates were cleaved by <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA in buffer A, but not in buffer B (lanes 2 and 9 versus 7 and 14). The incubation time (at 37&#176;C) was 10 min (lanes 1 and 8), 1 h (lanes 4, 6, 11 and 13), or 20 h (lanes 2, 5, 7, 9, 12 and 14). In lanes 3 and 10, a 5&#8242;-end-labeled 6-mer oligoribonucleotide (pCCCUUU) served as size control to assign cleavage at the m<sub>&#8722;</sub><sub>1</sub> site.</p>

(<bold>A</bold>) Time courses for cleavage in the presence of 5 &#181;M <italic>B. subtilis</italic> P RNA, &lt;1 nM ptRNA, 1 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc, 50 mM MES, pH 5.5 and 120 mM Mg<sup>2+</sup>, with the two cleavage sites (c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>+1</sub>) indicated at the right margin. (<bold>B</bold>) Processing of the same three substrates by the <italic>B. subtilis</italic> RNase P holoenzyme (lanes 13&#8211;18) in buffer B (see legend to <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>); as size reference, corresponding reactions catalyzed by <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA in buffer A (see legend to <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>) were loaded (lanes 7&#8211;12); control incubations for 20 h in the absence of enzyme were performed in buffer B (lanes 1&#8211;3) or buffer A (lanes 4&#8211;6). ###xml 4130 5613 4082 5549 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="26">Processing of the LNA (T-1) substrate by <italic>E. coli</italic> P RNA at different Mg<sup>2+</sup> concentrations. (<bold>A&#8211;D</bold>) Kinetic analyses of the two parallel cleavage pathways leading to cleavage at site c<sub>0</sub> or m<sub>+1</sub>. Cleavage experiments were performed under single turnover conditions (5 &#181;M P RNA, &lt;1 nM ptRNA) in the presence of 1 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc, 50 mM PIPES, pH 7 and 60 mM Mg<sup>2+</sup>. Plots representing selected Mg<sup>2+</sup> concentrations show cleavage at the canonical c<sub>0</sub> site (open circles) and site m<sub>+1</sub> (filled triangles). The fraction of substrate reacted is expressed as the ratio of product at a given time [<italic>P</italic>] to the total amount of substrate [<italic>S</italic>]<sub>tot</sub> at the start of the reaction. The relative amount of cleavage taking place at the canonical site (<italic>F</italic><sub>c</sub>; open squares) was calculated as the amount of c<sub>0</sub> product divided by the sum of c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>+1</sub> cleavage products. (<bold>E</bold>) Observed rate constants for cleavage at sites c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>+1</sub> as a function of Mg<sup>2+</sup> concentration. Data were fitted to the Hill equation: <italic>k</italic><sub>obs</sub> = (<italic>V</italic><sub>max</sub> &#8226; [Mg<sup>2+</sup>]<italic><sup>n</sup></italic>)/(<italic>K</italic>&#8242;+[Mg<sup>2+</sup>]<italic><sup>n</sup></italic>), resulting in reasonable fits with <italic>V</italic><sub>max</sub> = 0.08 &#177; 0.003, <italic>K</italic>&#8242; = 0.066 &#177; 0.02 and <italic>n</italic> = 1.61 &#177; 0.12 for c<sub>0</sub> cleavage, and <italic>V</italic><sub>max</sub> = 0.054 &#177; 0.003, <italic>K</italic>&#8242; = 0.03 &#177; 0.017 and <italic>n</italic> = 1.71 &#177; 0.21 for m<sub>+1</sub> cleavage; <italic>K</italic><sub>1/2</sub> values were calculated as <inline-formula><inline-graphic xlink:href="gkp775i1.jpg"/></inline-formula> for c<sub>0</sub> and 129 mM for m<sub>+1</sub> cleavage. (<bold>F</bold>) Double logarithmic presentation of the data shown in panel E to illustrate that cleavage at site c<sub>0</sub> was slower at low Mg<sup>2+</sup> concentrations but faster at high Mg<sup>2+</sup> concentrations relative to m<sub>+1</sub> cleavage.</p>

###xml 113 120 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 124 135 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 169 176 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 180 191 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 1160 1164 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 1325 1329 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 1332 1336 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 1654 1661 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2181 2188 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2387 2394 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2455 2462 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2526 2533 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2710 2717 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2891 2898 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 3311 3322 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 3341 3352 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 3431 3442 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 3633 3644 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 3772 3779 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 4171 4178 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 5097 5101 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
The ptRNA variants were processed under single turnover conditions at saturating enzyme concentrations (5 microM E. coli or B. subtilis P RNA or 100 nM of reconstituted E. coli or B. subtilis RNase P holoenzyme), 1 M NH4OAc (for RNA-alone reactions) or 0.1 M KCl (for holoenzyme reactions), and at Mg2+ concentrations and pH conditions as specified. The pH of 7.0 was chosen to provide conditions where substantial cleavage of all variants occurred, even at low Mg2+ concentrations; pH values of 5.5 or 6.0 allowed us to analyze cleavage at rate-limiting chemistry for all substrates (9). All processing reactions were performed at 37degreesC, P RNA solutions were preincubated for 1 h at 37degreesC and ptRNA solutions for 5 min at 55degreesC and 25 min at 37degreesC before mixing the two. For holoenzyme kinetics, an additional enzyme reconstitution procedure was included (see above). Aliquots withdrawn at different time points from enzyme-substrate mixtures were subjected to ethanol precipitation in the presence of 20 microg of glycogen before analysis by 20% PAGE/8 M urea. Data analysis and calculation of single turnover rate constants of cleavage (kobs) was performed as described (32). For the Mg2+ titration experiments in Figure 4E, data were analyzed by non-linear regression analysis using the Hill equation kobs = kobs, max * [Mg2+]n/(K' + [Mg2+]n). Figure 2.Analysis of RNase P cleavage site selection; (A) Secondary structure of ptRNA acceptor stem ends; arrows assign the different RNase P (RNA) cleavage sites: c0, canonical site; m-1, m+1, aberrant sites. (B) Cleavage of ptRNA variants LNA (T-1), 2'-OCH3 (T-1) and 2'-OH (T-1) by E. coli P RNA (lanes 2, 4 and 6) and cleavage of the corresponding 24-mers (Figure 1A) used to construct the ptRNA variants by nuclease P1 (lanes 1, 3 and 5). Numbers on the left side indicate the length (nt) of fragments generated by nuclease P1; the corresponding P RNA cleavage sites are indicated in parentheses. The rectangles mark the missing or reduced P1 fragments due to the absence of a 2'-OH at the corresponding position. Hydrolysis by nuclease P1 was performed as described in the 'Materials and Methods' section. E. coli P RNA cleavage was performed in buffer A (1 M NH4OAc, 50 mM PIPES, pH 7 and 20 mM Mg2+) for 8 h (lane 2), 22 h (lane 4) and 10 min (lane 6) at 37degreesC. (C) Analysis of cleavage site selection by E. coli P RNA and holoenzyme. In lanes 1, 2, 8 and 9, processing by E. coli P RNA was performed in buffer A as in panel B; cleavage by the E. coli holoenzyme (lanes 4, 5, 11 and 12) was conducted in buffer B (50 mM MES, pH 6, 0.1 M KCl and 10 mM MgCl2); we also included control reactions in buffer B in the absence of the E. coli protein subunit (lanes 6, 7, 13 and 14), which illustrate the requirement for the protein cofactor under low salt conditions: the LNA and 2'-OCH3 substrates were cleaved by E. coli P RNA in buffer A, but not in buffer B (lanes 2 and 9 versus 7 and 14). The incubation time (at 37degreesC) was 10 min (lanes 1 and 8), 1 h (lanes 4, 6, 11 and 13), or 20 h (lanes 2, 5, 7, 9, 12 and 14). In lanes 3 and 10, a 5'-end-labeled 6-mer oligoribonucleotide (pCCCUUU) served as size control to assign cleavage at the m-1 site.Figure 3.Processing of ptRNAs 2'-OH (T-1), 2'-OCH3 (T-1) and LNA (T-1) by (A) B. subtilis P RNA and (B) the B. subtilis RNase P holoenzyme. (A) Time courses for cleavage in the presence of 5 microM B. subtilis P RNA, <1 nM ptRNA, 1 M NH4OAc, 50 mM MES, pH 5.5 and 120 mM Mg2+, with the two cleavage sites (c0 and m+1) indicated at the right margin. (B) Processing of the same three substrates by the B. subtilis RNase P holoenzyme (lanes 13-18) in buffer B (see legend to Figure 2); as size reference, corresponding reactions catalyzed by E. coli P RNA in buffer A (see legend to Figure 2) were loaded (lanes 7-12); control incubations for 20 h in the absence of enzyme were performed in buffer B (lanes 1-3) or buffer A (lanes 4-6). Incubation times were 5 min (lane 7), 20 min (lane 8), 10 min (lane 13), 30 min (lane 14), 4 h (lanes 9, 11, 15, 17) and 20 h (lanes 1-6, 10, 12, 16, 18).Figure 4.Processing of the LNA (T-1) substrate by E. coli P RNA at different Mg2+ concentrations. (A-D) Kinetic analyses of the two parallel cleavage pathways leading to cleavage at site c0 or m+1. Cleavage experiments were performed under single turnover conditions (5 microM P RNA, <1 nM ptRNA) in the presence of 1 M NH4OAc, 50 mM PIPES, pH 7 and 60 mM Mg2+. Plots representing selected Mg2+ concentrations show cleavage at the canonical c0 site (open circles) and site m+1 (filled triangles). The fraction of substrate reacted is expressed as the ratio of product at a given time [P] to the total amount of substrate [S]tot at the start of the reaction. The relative amount of cleavage taking place at the canonical site (Fc; open squares) was calculated as the amount of c0 product divided by the sum of c0 and m+1 cleavage products. (E) Observed rate constants for cleavage at sites c0 and m+1 as a function of Mg2+ concentration. Data were fitted to the Hill equation: kobs = (Vmax * [Mg2+]n)/(K'+[Mg2+]n), resulting in reasonable fits with Vmax = 0.08 +/- 0.003, K' = 0.066 +/- 0.02 and n = 1.61 +/- 0.12 for c0 cleavage, and Vmax = 0.054 +/- 0.003, K' = 0.03 +/- 0.017 and n = 1.71 +/- 0.21 for m+1 cleavage; K1/2 values were calculated as  for c0 and 129 mM for m+1 cleavage. (F) Double logarithmic presentation of the data shown in panel E to illustrate that cleavage at site c0 was slower at low Mg2+ concentrations but faster at high Mg2+ concentrations relative to m+1 cleavage.

###xml 1514 1521 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Analysis of RNase P cleavage site selection; (A) Secondary structure of ptRNA acceptor stem ends; arrows assign the different RNase P (RNA) cleavage sites: c0, canonical site; m-1, m+1, aberrant sites. (B) Cleavage of ptRNA variants LNA (T-1), 2'-OCH3 (T-1) and 2'-OH (T-1) by E. coli P RNA (lanes 2, 4 and 6) and cleavage of the corresponding 24-mers (Figure 1A) used to construct the ptRNA variants by nuclease P1 (lanes 1, 3 and 5). Numbers on the left side indicate the length (nt) of fragments generated by nuclease P1; the corresponding P RNA cleavage sites are indicated in parentheses. The rectangles mark the missing or reduced P1 fragments due to the absence of a 2'-OH at the corresponding position. Hydrolysis by nuclease P1 was performed as described in the 'Materials and Methods' section. E. coli P RNA cleavage was performed in buffer A (1 M NH4OAc, 50 mM PIPES, pH 7 and 20 mM Mg2+) for 8 h (lane 2), 22 h (lane 4) and 10 min (lane 6) at 37degreesC. (C) Analysis of cleavage site selection by E. coli P RNA and holoenzyme. In lanes 1, 2, 8 and 9, processing by E. coli P RNA was performed in buffer A as in panel B; cleavage by the E. coli holoenzyme (lanes 4, 5, 11 and 12) was conducted in buffer B (50 mM MES, pH 6, 0.1 M KCl and 10 mM MgCl2); we also included control reactions in buffer B in the absence of the E. coli protein subunit (lanes 6, 7, 13 and 14), which illustrate the requirement for the protein cofactor under low salt conditions: the LNA and 2'-OCH3 substrates were cleaved by E. coli P RNA in buffer A, but not in buffer B (lanes 2 and 9 versus 7 and 14). The incubation time (at 37degreesC) was 10 min (lanes 1 and 8), 1 h (lanes 4, 6, 11 and 13), or 20 h (lanes 2, 5, 7, 9, 12 and 14). In lanes 3 and 10, a 5'-end-labeled 6-mer oligoribonucleotide (pCCCUUU) served as size control to assign cleavage at the m-1 site.

###xml 41 48 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 967 971 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
Processing of the LNA (T-1) substrate by E. coli P RNA at different Mg2+ concentrations. (A-D) Kinetic analyses of the two parallel cleavage pathways leading to cleavage at site c0 or m+1. Cleavage experiments were performed under single turnover conditions (5 microM P RNA, <1 nM ptRNA) in the presence of 1 M NH4OAc, 50 mM PIPES, pH 7 and 60 mM Mg2+. Plots representing selected Mg2+ concentrations show cleavage at the canonical c0 site (open circles) and site m+1 (filled triangles). The fraction of substrate reacted is expressed as the ratio of product at a given time [P] to the total amount of substrate [S]tot at the start of the reaction. The relative amount of cleavage taking place at the canonical site (Fc; open squares) was calculated as the amount of c0 product divided by the sum of c0 and m+1 cleavage products. (E) Observed rate constants for cleavage at sites c0 and m+1 as a function of Mg2+ concentration. Data were fitted to the Hill equation: kobs = (Vmax * [Mg2+]n)/(K'+[Mg2+]n), resulting in reasonable fits with Vmax = 0.08 +/- 0.003, K' = 0.066 +/- 0.02 and n = 1.61 +/- 0.12 for c0 cleavage, and Vmax = 0.054 +/- 0.003, K' = 0.03 +/- 0.017 and n = 1.71 +/- 0.21 for m+1 cleavage; K1/2 values were calculated as  for c0 and 129 mM for m+1 cleavage. (F) Double logarithmic presentation of the data shown in panel E to illustrate that cleavage at site c0 was slower at low Mg2+ concentrations but faster at high Mg2+ concentrations relative to m+1 cleavage.
###end p 26

ptRNA binding by spin column assays
###end title 27
###begin p 28
###xml 80 81 80 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 81 82 81 82 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 143 145 143 145 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 228 229 228 229 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 238 239 238 239 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 255 256 255 256 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 419 420 419 420 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 435 436 435 436 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
Spin column assays for the determination of equilibrium dissociation constants (Kd) of enzyme-substrate complexes were performed as described (10). Binding of ptRNAs to P RNA was analyzed in a buffer containing 50 mM MES, 1 M NH4OAc, CaCl2 (15 mM) or SrCl2 (5 or 80 mM), 0.1 % (w/v) SDS, 0.05 % (w/v) Nonidet P40, pH 6.0. Binding of ptRNAs to holoenzymes was analyzed in a buffer containing 50 mM Tris-acetate, 0.2 M NH4OAc, 15 mM CaCl2, 0.05 % (w/v) Nonidet P40, pH 7.1.
###end p 28
###begin title 29
RESULTS
###end title 29
###begin p 30
###xml 19 22 19 22 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 183 191 183 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 379 386 379 386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 403 407 403 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">endo</italic>
###xml 496 504 496 504 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 604 611 604 611 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 616 627 616 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 783 788 783 788 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33 B34 B35 B36 B37">33&#8211;37</xref>
###xml 604 611 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 616 627 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
The bacterial ptRNAGly variants with single modifications at nt -1 were constructed by ligation in the D loop after annealing of a synthetic 24-mer to a 5'-truncated tRNA transcript (Figure 1A). The different 2'-ribose modifications at nt -1 are illustrated in the boxes on the left. Several physico-chemical properties of the 2'-substituents investigated here are summarized in Table 1. The locked C3'-endo conformation of an LNA residue is shown in comparison to that of regular nucleotides in Figure 1B. To put our data into a broader perspective, we analyzed the substrates in reactions catalyzed by E. coli and B. subtilis RNase P (RNA), the main model systems for the two structurally distinct classes of bacterial P RNAs, type A (for 'ancestral') and type B (for 'Bacillus') (33-37).
###end p 30

###xml 57 64 57 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>

Effect of modifications at nt -1 on substrate binding by E. coli P RNA

###begin p 32
###xml 29 32 29 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 129 130 129 130 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 195 196 195 196 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 692 693 692 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 693 694 693 694 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 716 719 716 719 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 732 739 732 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>

###xml 3280 3282 3202 3204 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 3319 3320 3241 3242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 3320 3321 3242 3243 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 3388 3390 3310 3312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 2767 3392 2689 3314 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="34">The analysis of ptRNA binding was performed using the spin column assay (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>). The dissociation constant (<italic>K</italic><sub>d</sub>) was measured in the presence of 50 mM MES/NaOH, pH 6.0, 1 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc (P RNA) and Ca<sup>2+</sup> (15 mM) or Sr<sup>2+</sup> (5 or 80 mM) as the divalent metal ion; ptRNA binding to the holoenzyme was assayed at 50 mM Tris/CH<sub>3</sub>COOH, 0.2 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc, 15 mM Ca<sup>2+</sup>, pH 7.1. Relative <italic>K</italic><sub>d</sub> values (<italic>K</italic><sub>d,rel</sub>): individual <italic>K</italic><sub>d</sub> divided by <italic>K</italic><sub>d</sub> for the corresponding all-ribose ptRNA. <italic>K</italic><sub>d</sub> values for the 2&#8242;-F (C-1) and 2&#8242;-H (C-1) substrates at 15 mM Ca<sup>2+</sup> are consistent (within 2-fold) with <italic>K</italic><sub>d</sub> values determined in a previous study under identical conditions (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>).</p>
###xml 2767 3392 2689 3314 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF3"><p textid="34">The analysis of ptRNA binding was performed using the spin column assay (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>). ###xml 732 739 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 863 870 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1086 1093 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1677 1684 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1734 1741 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1746 1757 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Two sets of variants of ptRNAGly were investigated. The first set carried ribothymidines (rT) at nt -1 and -2 and a 2'-OH, 2'-OCH3 or LNA modification at nt -1 [referred to as 2'-OH (T-1), 2'-OCH3 (T-1) and LNA (T-1)] or LNA at nt -2 [LNA (T-2)]. The ribothymidines at positions -1 and -2 were introduced for reasons of comparability with variants carrying LNA substitutions at nt -1 or -2, because LNA analogs for uridine were not available. The second set of substrates carried a C at nt -1 and U at nt -2, and a 2'-OH, 2'-fluoro (2'-F) or 2'-deoxy (2'-H) substituent at position -1 [referred to as 2'-OH (C-1), 2'-F (C-1) and 2'-H (C-1)]. We determined equilibrium dissociation constants (Kd) for binding of ptRNAGly variants to E. coli P RNA at two Sr2+ (5 and 80 mM) and one Ca2+ (15 mM) concentration (Table 2). Both metal ions support substrate binding to E. coli P RNA with similar efficiency as Mg2+, but are inactive (Sr2+) or very inefficient (Ca2+) as catalytic cofactors [(30) and references therein]. The ptRNA with rT residues at -2 and -1, variant 2'-OH (T-1), bound to E. coli P RNA with the same affinity (within 2-fold) as the variant with U at -2 and C at -1, variant 2'-OH (C-1) (Table 2), indicating that the extra methyl groups on the bases as well as the pyrimidine identity at nt -1 had no or very marginal effects on substrate binding in the ground state. This essentially pertains to the LNA (T-2) substrate as well, which differed from the control substrate 2'-OH (T-1) only by a 3-4-fold increase in Kd at the lowest divalent metal ion concentration (5 mM Sr2+). Thus, an LNA modification at nucleotide -2 had little effect on substrate binding by E. coli P RNA. ###begin p 34
###xml 73 75 73 75 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 105 106 105 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 106 107 106 107 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 171 172 171 172 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 190 192 190 192 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 206 208 206 208 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 309 310 309 310 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 338 340 338 340 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 359 360 359 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 360 361 360 361 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 370 371 370 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 371 376 371 376 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d,rel</sub>
###xml 390 391 390 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 391 392 391 392 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 404 405 404 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 405 406 405 406 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 447 448 447 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 448 449 448 449 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 513 515 513 515 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 552 553 552 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 553 554 553 554 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 621 623 621 623 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
The analysis of ptRNA binding was performed using the spin column assay (10). The dissociation constant (Kd) was measured in the presence of 50 mM MES/NaOH, pH 6.0, 1 M NH4OAc (P RNA) and Ca2+ (15 mM) or Sr2+ (5 or 80 mM) as the divalent metal ion; ptRNA binding to the holoenzyme was assayed at 50 mM Tris/CH3COOH, 0.2 M NH4OAc, 15 mM Ca2+, pH 7.1. Relative Kd values (Kd,rel): individual Kd divided by Kd for the corresponding all-ribose ptRNA. Kd values for the 2'-F (C-1) and 2'-H (C-1) substrates at 15 mM Ca2+ are consistent (within 2-fold) with Kd values determined in a previous study under identical conditions (20).
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 155 156 155 156 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 286 288 286 288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 304 311 304 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 498 499 498 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 499 500 499 500 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 686 690 686 690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">endo</italic>
###xml 736 737 736 737 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 909 911 909 911 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1359 1360 1359 1360 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1421 1422 1421 1422 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
At all three tested metal ion conditions, binding defects were seen for the 2'-F (C-1) (2-4-fold), LNA (T-1) (2-13-fold), 2'-H (C-1) (9-60-fold) and 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrate (30-50-fold). Remarkably, the binding defect for LNA (T-1) was essentially suppressed (within 3-fold) at 15 mM Ca2+ or 80 mM Sr2+ (Table 2). For comparison, the 2'-H (C-1) ptRNA was still bound with 9-11-fold reduced affinity under the same conditions, thus even exceeding the defect of a 2'-F substitution (4-fold effect on Kd). In summary, the LNA substitution at position -1 had only a very minor impact on ptRNA ground state binding, despite its bulky extra methylene group and a sugar pucker arrested in C3'-endo. In contrast, the structurally related 2'-OCH3 modification caused a >30-fold affinity decrease at all tested metal ion concentrations. The 2'-deoxy substitution caused the largest affinity decrease, 60-fold at 5 mM Sr2+, which could be mitigated to 10-fold at the higher divalent metal ion concentrations. From the comparison of an LNA versus 2'-H and 2'-F modification at nt -1 we infer that the presence of a 2'-substituent at nt -1 with good H-bond acceptor capacity, such as the 2'-oxygen, is a major determinant for metal-dependent formation of E-S ground state complexes. Such information could not be extracted from the results obtained with the related 2'-OCH3 modification, because the steric effect dominates for 2'-OCH3.
###end p 35
###begin title 36
###xml 57 68 57 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 57 68 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Effect of modifications at nt -1 on substrate binding by B. subtilis P RNA
###end title 36
###begin p 37
###xml 0 11 0 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 69 71 69 71 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 108 115 108 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 123 130 123 130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 168 170 168 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 320 321 320 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 321 322 321 322 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 385 386 385 386 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 414 415 414 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 415 416 415 416 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 638 645 638 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 707 718 707 718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 0 11 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 108 115 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 638 645 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 707 718 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
B. subtilis P RNA bound the control all-ribose substrates at 15 mM Ca2+ with 19-26-fold lower affinity than E. coli P RNA (Table 2), consistent with previous findings (37). Again, whereas the LNA (T-1) substrate showed little perturbation of substrate binding relative to the 2'-OH (T-1) substrate (2.6-fold increase in Kd), the defect was most pronounced for the substrate with 2'-OCH3 at -1 (11-fold increase in Kd). Here, the 2'-H substitution reduced affinity only 2-fold and a 2'-F substituent was bound with roughly equal affinity as the 2'-OH (C-1) control substrate. These results are qualitatively similar to those obtained with E. coli P RNA, except for the generally weaker substrate affinity of B. subtilis P RNA and its relatively low apparent sensitivity to the 2'-H substitution at C-1.
###end p 37
###begin title 38
Effect of modifications at nt -1 on substrate binding by RNase P holoenzymes
###end title 38
###begin p 39
###xml 62 69 62 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 74 85 74 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 117 119 117 119 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 303 304 303 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 304 305 304 305 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 334 341 334 341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 401 408 401 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 421 432 421 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 555 566 555 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 623 624 623 624 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 655 662 655 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 677 688 677 688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 753 764 753 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 62 69 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 74 85 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 401 408 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 421 432 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 555 566 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 655 662 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 677 688 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 753 764 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
We further investigated binding of the modified substrates to E. coli and B. subtilis RNase P holoenzymes at 15 mM Ca2+ but in the presence of a 5-fold lower monovalent salt concentration (0.2 M) than in RNA-alone assays. The presence of the protein cofactor increased and equalized substrate affinity (Kd values between 1 and 13 nM; Table 2) and abolished the substrate affinity differences seen for E. coli relative to B. subtilis P RNA. The 2'-H (C-1) ptRNA was exceptional, as it was bound with 6-fold lower affinity than its control substrate by the B. subtilis holoenzyme, thus even exceeding the defect of the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrate (3.5-fold for E. coli, 4.1-fold for B. subtilis RNase P). Thus, a pronounced defect of 2'-H, not evident in the B. subtilis P RNA-alone affinity assay, emerged in the holoenzyme context. LNA at nt -1 affected ground state binding to the holoenzymes insignificantly.
###end p 39
###begin title 40
Cleavage site selection
###end title 40
###begin p 41
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 202 204 202 204 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sub>
###xml 263 264 263 264 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 303 305 303 305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 347 349 347 349 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 427 434 427 434 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 439 450 439 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 458 466 458 466 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 470 471 470 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 472 474 472 474 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 475 477 475 477 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 0 16 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 427 434 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 439 450 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Escherichia coli P RNA is known to form alternative E-S complexes in response to structural changes in the enzyme and/or substrate RNA, which lead to aberrant cleavage usually one nucleotide upstream (m-1 site, between -2 and -1) of the canonical cleavage site (c0 site, between -1 and +1) (see e.g. 14,27). More rarely, aberrant cleavage at the m+1 site (between nt +1 and +2) has also been observed in reactions catalyzed by E. coli and B. subtilis P RNA (Figure 2A) (8,19,22).
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 35 36 35 36 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 84 91 84 91 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 127 128 127 128 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 137 144 137 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 216 217 216 217 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 380 387 380 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 458 459 458 459 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 465 467 465 467 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 475 483 475 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 540 541 540 541 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 586 588 586 588 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 595 603 595 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 732 733 732 733 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 740 748 740 748 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 831 839 831 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 992 994 992 994 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 995 997 995 997 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 137 144 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 380 387 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Except for the LNA (T-1) and 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrates, all ptRNA variants listed in Table 2 were processed exclusively at the c0 site by E. coli P RNA (data not shown). The cleavage sites for ptRNA with LNA or 2'-OCH3 at -1 were analyzed by co-electrophoresis of nuclease P1 hydrolysis ladders (P1 like RNase P generates 5'-phosphate termini) along with the products derived from E. coli P RNA cleavage. This revealed cleavage of the LNA (T-1) ptRNA at the c0 and m+1 sites (Figure 2B and C, lanes 2 and 9, respectively), whereas the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA was cleaved exclusively at the m+1 site (Figure 2B and C, lanes 4 and 2, respectively). The 7-nt 5'-cleavage product with the 3'-terminal LNA sugar generated by cleavage at the c0 site (Figure 2B, lane 2) migrated somewhat faster than the corresponding all-ribose counterpart (Figure 2B, lane 6). Changes in the mobility of short oligonucleotides with 3'-terminal ribose modifications in high-resolution gels have been documented before (20,22).
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 4 11 4 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 63 64 63 64 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 141 149 141 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 294 295 294 295 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 362 370 362 370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 550 551 550 551 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 675 676 675 676 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 739 740 739 740 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 740 741 740 741 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 763 765 763 765 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 801 809 801 809 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 865 872 865 872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 944 945 944 945 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 951 953 951 953 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 1022 1023 1022 1023 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 1023 1024 1023 1024 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1031 1039 1031 1039 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1091 1092 1091 1092 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1184 1191 1184 1191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1227 1235 1227 1235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1341 1344 1341 1344 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 1550 1552 1550 1552 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 1800 1805 1800 1805 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38 B39 B40">38&#8211;40</xref>
###xml 4 11 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 865 872 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1184 1191 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The E. coli RNase P holoenzyme cleaved the LNA (T-1) and 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNAs with very low efficiency relative to the unmodified substrate (Figure 2C, lanes 5 and 12 versus 4 and 11). Under the applied holoenzyme assay conditions (buffer B), essentially no cleavage of the LNA (T-1) and 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrates was seen in the absence of the protein cofactor (Figure 2C, lanes 7 and 14). Thus, the protein exerted its known effect, i.e. improvement of activity under low salt conditions, but a severe catalytic defect caused by LNA (T-1) and 2'-OCH3 at nt -1 remained despite the presence of the protein. Interestingly, the protein switched the cleavage site for the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA such that cleavage occurred predominantly at the m-1 site and not at the m+1 site as in the RNA-alone reaction (Figure 2C, lanes 2 versus 5). As in the RNA-alone reaction, the E. coli holoenzyme cleaved the LNA (T-1) substrate with low efficiency at the c0 and m+1 sites, and overexposure of gels even revealed some cleavage at the m-1 site (Figure 2C, lane 12). Processing inhibition by LNA and 2'-OCH3 at -1 also led to appearance of an aberrant cleavage product in reactions catalyzed by the E. coli holoenzyme (marked by asterisks in Figure 2C, lanes 5 and 12). This aberrant cleavage site, attributable to a minor alternative conformation of ptRNAGly, was tentatively assigned (data not shown) to the anticodon arm. Indeed, cleavage of such weakly populated aberrant tRNA conformers was observed before by Kikuchi and coworkers and termed hyperprocessing (38). The underlying rearrangement of the tRNA structure apparently results from base pairing between the 3'-strand of the acceptor stem and nucleotides of the variable loop and/or the 3'-strand of the anticodon stem to form a hairpin-like structure (38-40).
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 28 39 28 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 96 97 96 97 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>

###xml 215 226 215 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 247 255 247 255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 278 289 278 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 302 310 302 310 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 370 377 370 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 382 393 382 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 532 534 532 534 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 560 561 560 561 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 587 588 587 588 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 645 646 645 646 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 655 666 655 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 697 704 697 704 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 737 739 737 739 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 753 760 753 760 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 798 799 798 799 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 799 800 799 800 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 816 818 816 818 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 28 39 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 215 226 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 278 289 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 370 377 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 382 393 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 655 666 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 697 704 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 753 760 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In the reaction catayzed by B. subtilis P RNA and holoenzyme, we saw very weak cleavage at the c0 site for 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA and at the m+1 and c0 sites for LNA (T-1) ptRNA. Examples are shown in Figure 3 for the B. subtilis RNA-alone reaction (Figure 3A, lanes 6-15) and the B. subtilis holoenzyme (Figure 3B, lanes 15-18). In conclusion, all four tested activities (E. coli and B. subtilis P RNAs and holoenzymes) cleaved the LNA (T-1) substrate with very low efficiency relative to unmodified ptRNA, and utilized the aberrant m+1 site in addition to the c0 site. However, the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA was cleaved with very low effciency at the c0 site by B. subtilis P RNA and holoenzyme, whereas E. coli P RNA selected exclusively the m+1 site and the E. coli holoenzyme cleaved predominantly at m-1 and weakly at m+1.
###end p 44

###xml 96 103 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1361 1365 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 1437 1444 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1520 1524 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 2528 2535 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2931 2935 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
All modifications introduced at nt -1 significantly affected the cleavage reaction catalyzed by E. coli P RNA. The rate constants for c0 cleavage under single turnover conditions (E >> S) and rate-limiting chemistry (120 mM Mg2+, pH 5.5) decreased in the order 2'-OH (T-1) approximately LNA (T-2) approximately 2'-OH (C-1) > 2'-F (C-1) > 2'-H (C-1) >> LNA (T-1), and for the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA no cleavage at all was detected at the c0 site (Table 3). The same hierarchy was seen at 20 mM Mg2+, pH 5.5, but at this lower Mg2+ concentration cleavage of the LNA (T-1) and 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrates was at the detection limit and thus not further analyzed. Rate differences were mitigated at pH 7 and 120 mM Mg2+, which was expected because at this higher pH value cleavage rates are generally faster, but another step than cleavage chemistry begins to limit the turnover of ptRNA substrates with 2'-OH at nt -1 (20). At lower Mg2+ concentrations (20 mM), the defects owing to ribose modifications at nt -1 were exacerbated, consistent with the documented Mg2+ binding defect caused by the absence of the 2'-hydroxyl group at this location (8,20). Low efficiency cleavage of ptRNA 2'-OCH3 (T-1) at the m+1 site was comparable at 20 and 120 mM Mg2+ (pH 7), although the endpoint of the reaction was lower at 20 mM Mg2+ (0.3 versus 0.55, Table 3). ###xml 2142 2153 2092 2103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 2180 2181 2130 2131 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 2210 2212 2160 2162 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 2324 2326 2274 2276 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 2328 2347 2278 2297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli/B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 2504 2505 2454 2455 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 2511 2512 2461 2462 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 2512 2513 2462 2463 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 2544 2545 2494 2495 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 2576 2577 2526 2527 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 2583 2585 2533 2535 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 2677 2678 2627 2628 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 2699 2700 2649 2650 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 2034 2933 1988 2883 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="55">n.d.: Cleavage not detectable. Cleavage experiments were performed under the following conditions: 5 &#181;M <italic>B. subtilis</italic> P RNA, &lt;1 nM ptRNA, 1 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc, 50 mM MES, pH 5.5 and Mg<sup>2+</sup> as specified above each column or 100 nM holoenzyme, &lt;1 nM ptRNA, 100 mM KCl, 50 mM MES, pH 6 and 4 or 10 mM Mg<sup>2+</sup> (<italic>E. coli/B. subtilis</italic> holoenzyme). Holoenzyme reconstitution and kinetic experiments were performed as described under Materials and Methods. Cleavage is differentiated for the c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>&#8722;</sub><sub>1</sub> site in the case of the 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> (T-1) substrate, and for the c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>+1</sub> site in the case of ptRNA LNA (T-1); all other substrates were cleaved exclusively at the c<sub>0</sub> site. For the 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> (T-1) and LNA (T-1) substrates, cleavage occurred to very low extents [in most cases with saturation already reached at the first data point (1 h)]; thus, only the extent of cleavage instead of cleavage rate constants is given here.</p>
###xml 2034 2933 1988 2883 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF8"><p textid="55">n.d.: Cleavage not detectable. Cleavage experiments were performed under the following conditions: 5 &#181;M <italic>B. subtilis</italic> P RNA, &lt;1 nM ptRNA, 1 M NH<sub>4</sub>OAc, 50 mM MES, pH 5.5 and Mg<sup>2+</sup> as specified above each column or 100 nM holoenzyme, &lt;1 nM ptRNA, 100 mM KCl, 50 mM MES, pH 6 and 4 or 10 mM Mg<sup>2+</sup> (<italic>E. coli/B. subtilis</italic> holoenzyme). Holoenzyme reconstitution and kinetic experiments were performed as described under Materials and Methods. Cleavage is differentiated for the c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>&#8722;</sub><sub>1</sub> site in the case of the 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> (T-1) substrate, and for the c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>+1</sub> site in the case of ptRNA LNA (T-1); all other substrates were cleaved exclusively at the c<sub>0</sub> site. For the 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> (T-1) and LNA (T-1) substrates, cleavage occurred to very low extents [in most cases with saturation already reached at the first data point (1 h)]; thus, only the extent of cleavage instead of cleavage rate constants is given here.</p></fn>

Cleavage is differentiated for the c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>&#8722;</sub><sub>1</sub> site in the case of the 2&#8242;-OCH<sub>3</sub> (T-1) substrate, and for the c<sub>0</sub> and m<sub>+1</sub> site in the case of ptRNA LNA (T-1); all other substrates were cleaved exclusively at the c<sub>0</sub> site. ###xml 200 207 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 457 468 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 624 631 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 681 692 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 1052 1056 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 1128 1139 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 1150 1157 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1162 1173 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 1310 1314 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
###xml 2142 2153 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 2328 2335 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2336 2347 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
In single turnover reactions (5 microM P RNA) at 120 mM Mg2+ and rate-limiting chemistry (pH 5.5) (10), the hierarchy of effects caused by the different ribose modifications equaled that observed for E. coli P RNA (cf. Tables 3 and 4), but the decreases in rate constant were more pronounced for the 2'-F (C-1) and particularly the 2'-H (C-1) ptRNA analyzed under the same conditions. Furthermore, the endpoint for c0 cleavage of the LNA (T-1) substrate by B. subtilis P RNA was approximately2.5% (Table 4), compared with 65% (fitted endpoint) and 42% (highest substrate conversion measured experimentally; Table 3) for the E. coli P RNA reaction. Another peculiarity was seen for B. subtilis P RNA-catalyzed cleavage of 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA at the c0 site and LNA (T-1) ptRNA at the m+1-site. Here, cleavage was already at saturation at the first time point (1 h; Table 4 and Figure 3A, lanes 6-15), with very low endpoints (1-4%; Table 4). A possible explanation is that weakly populated E-S conformers gave rise to these cleavages. Cleavage experiments were performed under the following conditions: 5 microM B. subtilis P RNA, <1 nM ptRNA, 1 M NH4OAc, 50 mM MES, pH 5.5 and Mg2+ as specified above each column or 100 nM holoenzyme, <1 nM ptRNA, 100 mM KCl, 50 mM MES, pH 6 and 4 or 10 mM Mg2+ (E. coli/B. subtilis holoenzyme).
