###begin title 80
###xml 16 17 16 17 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 17 18 17 18 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
Suppression of m-1 cleavage
###end title 80
###begin p 81
###xml 37 38 37 38 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 84 91 84 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 106 107 106 107 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 115 123 115 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 189 191 189 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 314 325 314 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 350 351 350 351 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 384 385 384 385 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 385 386 385 386 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 627 628 627 628 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 672 673 672 673 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 673 674 673 674 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 681 683 681 683 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 684 686 684 686 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 729 730 729 730 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 730 731 730 731 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 759 760 759 760 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 823 825 823 825 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 826 828 826 828 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 873 875 873 875 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 884 891 884 891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 945 946 945 946 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1089 1097 1089 1097 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">Scheme 1</xref>
###xml 1144 1145 1144 1145 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sub>
###xml 1145 1146 1145 1146 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1155 1156 1155 1156 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 1156 1157 1156 1157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1176 1177 1176 1177 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1214 1221 1214 1221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1242 1250 1242 1250 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1376 1378 1376 1378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 84 91 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 314 325 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 884 891 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1214 1221 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Another idiosyncrasy of LNA or 2'-OCH3 at -1 is the complete absence of cleavage by E. coli P RNA at the m-1 site (Figure 2B and C), which represents the prevailing miscleavage site [e.g. (44)]. Pan and colleagues showed that a 2'-deoxy substitution at -1 in ptRNA not only decreased the cleavage rate constant by B. subtilis P RNA 240-fold for the c0 site but also 470-fold for the m-1 site and 210-fold for another aberrant site (between nt +2 and +3). This finding suggested a contact between the ribozyme and the ptRNA substrate 2'-OH at -1 which promotes a conformational rearrangement required for catalysis at both the c0 as well as at aberrant sites, such as the m-1 site (19,24). Blockage of cleavage at the unmodified m-1 site owing to LNA or 2'-OCH3 at -1 would be consistent with the findings of Loria and Pan (19,24). Based on their model, utilization of the m+1 site in E. coli P RNA-catalyzed cleavage of ptRNA LNA (T-1) or 2'-OCH3 (T-1) may suggest that the 2'-OH group at nt +1 took over the role of that at nt -1 in promoting the conformational step preceding catalysis (Scheme 1). Likewise, redirection of cleavage from the m+1 to the m-1 site in the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrate when cleaved by the E. coli RNase P holoenzyme (Figure 2C) may be due to the protein cofactor allowing utilization of the 2'-OH at nt -2 as anchor point for the conformational step (24).
###end p 81
###begin title 82
###xml 18 19 18 19 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 25 27 25 27 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 40 47 40 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 40 47 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
pH dependence of c0 and m+1 cleavage by E. coli P RNA
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 33 34 33 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 34 37 34 37 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">obs</sub>
###xml 59 61 59 61 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 242 244 242 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 245 247 245 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 293 294 293 294 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 297 298 297 298 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 298 299 298 299 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 302 304 302 304 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 537 538 537 538 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 732 733 732 733 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 762 770 762 770 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 33 37 <span type="species:ncbi:59530">kobs</span>
The shallow pH dependence of log kobs for cleavage at the m+1 site is consistent with one or more slow steps upstream of the hydrolysis step in the miscleavage pathway, such as conformational rearrangements. Our findings and those of others (22,45) indicate that cleavage at different sites (c0, m-1, m+1 or others) has different pH and metal ion dependencies and involves different contributions from rate-limiting steps. Accordingly, E-S complexes leading to cleavage at the different sites are structurally distinct. Cleavage at the c0 site has usually the highest apparent metal ion affinity, which still pertains to 'mild' modifications, such as 2'-deoxy at nt -1. However, more deleterious modifications, such as LNA or 2'-OCH3 at -1, can break this rule (Figure 4E). Considering that LNA at nt -1 had little effect on substrate binding in the ground state, this modification is a paradigm for a modification that specifically inhibits formation of later steps along the cleavage pathway.
###end p 83
###begin title 84
###xml 35 46 35 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 35 46 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Cleavage of modified substrates by B. subtilis P RNA
###end title 84
###begin p 85
###xml 15 17 15 17 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 57 60 57 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Phe</sup>
###xml 64 75 64 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 151 154 151 154 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 182 190 182 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 239 242 239 242 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Phe</sup>
###xml 265 266 265 266 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 266 267 266 267 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 385 396 385 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 423 426 423 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 518 520 518 520 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 527 534 527 534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T4">Table 4</xref>
###xml 552 553 552 553 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 600 601 600 601 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 608 616 608 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 634 641 634 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 729 740 729 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 769 772 769 772 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gly</sup>
###xml 853 856 853 856 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Phe</sup>
###xml 858 860 858 860 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 907 910 907 910 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Phe</sup>
###xml 1034 1045 1034 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 1050 1053 1050 1053 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Phe</sup>
###xml 46 51 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 64 75 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 385 396 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 634 641 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 729 740 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 842 847 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 896 901 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1034 1045 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Loria and Pan (19) have studied processing of yeast ptRNAPhe by B. subtilis P RNA, representing a tRNA with a canonical 7-bp acceptor stem as the ptRNAGly used in our investigation (Figure 1). They observed substantial miscleavage of ptRNAPhe, particularly at the m-1 site and even in the absence of any ribose modifications. In contrast, we did not observe significant miscleavage by B. subtilis P RNA for any of the ptRNAGly variants used here, except for the LNA (T-1) substrate which gave rise to cleavage at the m+1 site (Table 4). Even the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) variant was cleaved exclusively at the c0 site (Figure 3), in contrast to E. coli P RNA which entirely miscleaved this substrate. Thus, we observed little propensity of B. subtilis P RNA to miscleave the ptRNAGly substrate. The discrepancy to the previously observed miscleavage of yeast ptRNAPhe (19) may be explained by the fact that yeast ptRNAPhe has a rather labile acceptor stem with 3 A-U and 1 G-U bp in a row in its lower part; in comparison, the acceptor stems of B. subtilis tRNAPhe molecules consist of 6 G-C and a single A-U bp, which is more typical of bacterial tRNAs. Low rigidity of the tRNA body is expected to cause conformational heterogeneity, which would explain increased miscleavage. This further raises the question if miscleavage at a specific site necessarily proceeds along the same mechanistic pathway for ptRNAs with rigid and less rigid tRNA bodies.
###end p 85
###begin title 86
###xml 39 46 39 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 39 46 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Cleavage of modified substrates by the E. coli RNase P holoenzyme
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 90 97 90 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 221 223 221 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 224 226 224 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 316 318 316 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 427 434 427 434 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 495 496 495 496 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 496 497 496 497 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 535 536 535 536 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 543 545 543 545 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 90 97 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 427 434 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In several previous analyses, essentially identical miscleavage patterns were observed in E. coli P RNA-alone and holoenzyme reactions. This pertains, for example, to the disruption of the 3'-CCA interaction by mutation (36,46), or to reactions utilizing a A248U mutant P RNA and a ptRNA with a 2'-deoxy-U at nt -1 (41). However, in a study investigating the effect of a substrate 2'-amino modification at nt -1 on cleavage by E. coli RNase P (RNA), the P protein suppressed miscleavage at the m-1 site and redirected cleavage to the c0 site (21). This suggests that effects of the P protein on cleavage fidelity depend on the specific structural alteration.
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 31 32 31 32 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 87 89 87 89 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 98 99 98 99 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 99 100 99 100 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 113 120 113 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 161 169 161 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 232 233 232 233 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 289 297 289 297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 821 822 821 822 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 865 866 865 866 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sub>
###xml 866 867 866 867 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 913 915 913 915 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 1079 1087 1077 1085 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">Scheme 1</xref>
###xml 1110 1112 1108 1110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 113 120 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The cleavage site of the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrate was almost entirely shifted from the m+1 to the m-1 site in the E. coli holoenzyme versus P RNA-alone reaction (Figure 2C, lanes 2 and 5). With LNA at -1, also some cleavage at the m-1 site appeared in the presence of the protein cofactor (Figure 2C, lanes 9 and 12). Evidently, the protein, by providing additional substrate binding energy and by enhancing the affinity of key metal ions, modulates the activation barriers of pathways leading to cleavage at different sites. The differences in mono- and di-valent salt conditions used in RNA-alone and holoenzyme reactions may also have contributed to the observed protein-dependent changes, resulting in differential effects on the individual miscleavage pathways. Specifically, the shift of cleavage site for the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) substrate may be explained by (E*S)m-1 complex formation favored over that of (E*S)m+1 complexes in the context of the holoenzyme reaction, and/or by a differential effect of the protein on the individual equilibrium docking steps [(E*S) --> (E*S)*; Scheme 1] preceding catalysis (24). The protein might also affect active site architecture more profoundly than as yet thought.
###end p 88
###begin title 89
###xml 20 27 20 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 32 43 32 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 20 27 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 32 43 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
Differences between E. coli and B. subtilis RNase P (RNA)
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 108 110 108 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 161 172 161 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 322 329 322 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 339 341 339 341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 342 344 342 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 378 389 378 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 453 460 453 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 468 470 468 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 477 488 477 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 540 547 540 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 582 589 582 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 612 614 612 614 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 751 753 751 753 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 770 772 770 772 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 792 803 792 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 870 877 870 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 885 887 885 887 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 1137 1148 1137 1148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 1156 1163 1156 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1228 1229 1228 1229 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1314 1315 1314 1315 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1434 1435 1434 1435 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 1441 1443 1441 1443 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+1</sub>
###xml 161 172 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 322 329 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 378 389 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 453 460 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 477 488 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 540 547 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 582 589 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 792 803 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 870 877 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1137 1148 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 1156 1163 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Architectural differences between bacterial P RNAs of type A (for 'ancestral') and type B (for 'Bacillus') (33) are associated with biochemical differences. The B. subtilis RNase P holoenzyme binds ptRNA with a much higher affinity than mature tRNA, but this discrimination against mature tRNA is much less pronounced for E. coli RNase P (34,35). RNase P enzymes containing the B. subtilis P RNA are less prone to aberrant cleavage than those including E. coli P RNA (36), and B. subtilis P RNA alone binds ptRNA substrates weaker than its E. coli counterpart (37, this study). The E. coli protein reduces the Mg2+ concentration requirement for tertiary structure formation of P RNA and increases the melting temperature at physiologically relevant Mg2+ concentrations (37). In contrast, the B. subtilis protein does not exert such stabilizing effects on its cognate or E. coli P RNA (37). Taking these reported differences between the two RNase P model systems into account, it is not surprising that we saw differences and commonalities (for details, see Results). Differences included a stronger defect caused by 2'-H at nt -1 on the B. subtilis versus E. coli holoenzyme, and deviating cleavage site selection for the 2'-OCH3 substrate; major commonalities included the severe catalytic block by LNA and 2'-OCH3 and, for the LNA substrate, the occurrence of low efficiency parallel cleavage pathways leading to hydrolysis at the c0 and m+1 sites. The differences illustrate the complex interplay of functional groups and of thermodynamic as well as kinetic parameters in this RNA-catalyzed and protein-assisted phosphodiester hydrolysis reaction. Compared with protein enzyme orthologs with rigid and strongly conserved active sites, type A and B RNase P enzymes appear more as homologs that still catalyze the same reactions, but with distinct architectural and non-identical mechanistic concepts.
###end p 90
###begin title 91
The P protein is unable to compensate the catalytic block by LNA
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 87 89 87 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
###xml 90 92 90 92 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 134 136 134 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 181 183 181 183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 269 280 269 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 402 404 402 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 405 407 405 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 511 513 511 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 585 592 585 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 717 719 717 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 789 796 789 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1018 1020 1018 1020 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 1108 1109 1108 1109 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1151 1158 1151 1158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1163 1174 1163 1174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B. subtilis</italic>
###xml 1238 1245 1238 1245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1335 1336 1335 1336 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 269 280 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
###xml 585 592 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 789 796 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1151 1158 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1163 1174 <span type="species:ncbi:1423">B. subtilis</span>
The protein subunit of bacterial RNase P increases substrate affinity and specificity (47,48), stabilizes the local RNA conformation (37), preorganizes S- and C-domain orientation (24) and increases the affinity of catalytically important divalent metal ions (11). For B. subtilis, it has been shown that the P protein interacts with the 5'-leader of tRNA precursor thus increasing substrate affinity (37,49) while reducing the contact area to the T stem-loop region of tRNA substrates relative to P RNA alone (50). Recently, the binding affinity and processing efficiency of a set of E. coli ptRNA substrates with different 5'-leaders and bodies was investigated in the absence and presence of the protein cofactor (51). The results indicated that the protein confers the capacity to the E. coli RNase P holoenzyme to bind all 5'-pre-tRNAs with uniform affinity. Apparently, this capacity was achieved during evolution by combining suboptimal tRNA structures with 5'-leader sequences that confer high ptRNA affinity (51). Such a thermodynamic compensation effect was also seen here for binding of the 2'-OCH3 (T-1) ptRNA, where defects of binding to E. coli and B. subtilis P RNA were alleviated by the presence of the protein cofactor (Table 2). In contrast, the dramatic inhibitory effect on P RNA catalysis caused by LNA and 2'-OCH3 at nt -1 remained in the holoenzyme reaction, indicating that these modifications block E*S* formation and/or the bond breakage step itself. Finally, our results demonstrate that LNA enriches the nucleotide analog toolbox for mechanistic enzyme studies.
###end p 92
